When the proposal to take over the school for self-management was decided, it appointed a president, rectified the school name, and allocated funds, directing everything with composure, so that the teaching has not ceased to this day. Whose power is this? We must be grateful to Mr. Yuan Guanlan. Mr. Yuan, named Xitao, was from Baoshan County, Jiangsu Province. At that time, he was the Vice Minister of Education acting as the head of the ministry and was also a member of the Wartime International Affairs Committee. He was able to maintain our school with his utmost sincerity and great power, preventing it from falling. After leaving the government, he devoted himself to local education and used his remaining energy to oversee our school. Throughout his life, Mr. Yuan made many contributions to education, and his great virtues and great achievements are beyond words. But his contribution to our school is especially great. After his death, we write this article in the public interest to inform future generations. Mr. Yuan Guanlan died on August 29th, the 19th year of the Republic of China, at the age of sixty-five." Alumni Association of the National Tongji University.

Ban on the Manufacture of Old-Style Scales

Unification of Weights and Measures

Since the Social Bureau stipulated the standard of weights and measures, it has notified the scale shops in the city to manufacture according to the regulations on record. However, recently, it has been found that while there are many people in this industry who manufacture according to the regulations, there are also not a few who adhere to the old-style models. Therefore, in recent days, personnel have been sent to each of these industries to conduct thorough investigations and inspections. If any illegal old-style scales or similar items are found, they will be immediately abolished and ordered to manufacture according to the stipulated standard scale model in the future. If they resist or disobey, they will be immediately taken to the police stations in each district of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for punishment.

Cosmetics Association Seeks National Cosmetics Samples

To Transport Freshly and Display Widely for Promotion

The Shanghai Cosmetics Trade Association issued a notice to all factory members yesterday regarding the transportation of fresh national cosmetics samples for display, stating, "Dear Sirs, On the 11th of this month, a letter was approved from the Secretariat of the China National Products Maintenance Association, stating, 'It has been found that our country's goods sold to Korea used to reach tens of millions of yuan in the past. However, since Japan implemented harsh taxation on Chinese goods, taxing them at a rate of 100%, except for a small number of goods that can be sold, most goods, such as silk, have not been able to be shipped for years. The number of people in our country's industrial and commercial circles who have been devastated is no less than several million. Although the government has made efforts to negotiate and revise the tax rate to 70%, it is still too far apart compared to the 8% tax rate levied on Japanese goods. Fortunately, the term of this agreement is three years, and excluding the past year, it is only effective for two years. Our association plans to take advantage of this period to request the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to convene relevant industrial and commercial groups to conduct detailed research on the points that should be revised in this Sino-Japanese commercial treaty so that it can be submitted at the time and negotiated with Japan for proper handling. On the other hand, with the consent of Mr. Zhang Weicheng, the Consul General stationed in Korea, we are collecting samples of our country's exquisite national products and transporting them to the Consulate General stationed in Korea to select a site to establish a China National Products Exhibition Hall so that we can invite overseas Chinese and local people from all walks of life to visit the hall from time to time to make them understand and recognize and develop their faith and desire to purchase. This is the first step in preparing for the restoration of trade with Korea and is an essential task. Moreover, Consul General Zhang has returned to Shanghai on official business and will be staying for a few more days. Therefore, we are sending you this special letter to request that you quickly compile and number the samples of exquisite new and old goods, clearly state the factory name, location, trademark, value, etc., on a separate sheet of paper, and properly package them and send them to our association at Gaodun Street, Nine Acres, this port by the 25th of this month for inspection and collection so that they can be transferred to Consul General Zhang to be displayed fresh and restore their inherent glory and re-display the glory of the country. The time is short, and opportunity waits for no one. We hope that you will handle this as soon as possible and do not delay. We are deeply looking forward to it.' In view of this, our country's domestic cosmetic products are still in their infancy, and overseas trade has not been fully developed. We can take this opportunity to transport them freshly and promote them widely in order to arouse the patriotic sentiments of overseas Chinese and to recover the outflow of rights and interests, which will have considerable effect. Therefore, we are sending you this letter to request that your company quickly compile and number the samples of exquisite goods, clearly state the factory name, location, trademark, value, etc., on a separate sheet of paper, and properly package them and send them to our association for inspection and collection by the 24th of this month so that they can be compiled and transported fresh. We are eagerly awaiting your prompt action."

Local News Two

Jing'an Temple Fair on Buddha's Birthday

The Stall Setting Incident Resolved Satisfactorily

The Municipal Council Allowed to Follow Past Practice

The ancient Jing'an Temple is a famous scenic spot in western Shanghai with many historical sites. During the Buddha's Birthday temple fair (Bathing the Buddha Festival) each year, the temple is crowded with people burning incense and sightseeing. Thousands of farmers and workers from the interior gather to set up stalls to sell their self-made local products to earn a living, resembling an exhibition of national products and local specialties. This year, the Municipal Council issued a notice restricting stall settings, causing panic among the stall vendors. They specially organized a stall vendors' association and petitioned for assistance from various parties. The abbot of Jing'an Temple, Zhifa, has repeatedly negotiated, and Shanghai gentry Du Yuesheng and Gu Jiatang, as well as local gentry Wang Hancheng, Gong Yifei, Xu Wenyuan, and the Citizens' Federation, have warmly assisted. The temple received a reply from the Municipal Council yesterday, agreeing to consider the livelihoods of the common people and allowing stall settings according to past practice. The reply from the Municipal Council and the announcement from Jing'an Temple are recorded below.

Jing'an Temple Announcement Regarding the Announcement: This temple will hold a grand event on the eighth day of the fourth lunar month to commemorate the birthday of our Buddha Sakyamuni. The setting up of stalls by various vendors has been a long-standing practice. This year, the Municipal Council suddenly issued a notice restricting it. After repeated efforts to argue and negotiate with the Municipal Council by this temple, and with the assistance of various circles, the Municipal Council finally understood and agreed to allow stall settings according to past practice, from the third day to the ninth day of the fourth lunar month. We hope that all stall vendors will set up stalls and conduct business as usual. In addition to thanking all those who have assisted us, we are afraid that we have not informed everyone. This announcement is hereby made. Abbot Zhifa

Municipal Council Reply Dear Sirs, Your letter of May 7th regarding the issue of restricting stall settings has been received. The Municipal Council's order was to remedy the obstruction of traffic and public inconvenience at the temple fair in recent years. Now, because of the expression to the representatives of the vendors that it would disrupt their livelihoods, the Municipal Council has decided to extend the implementation of this order.

Sand and Mud Donation Collection Shipmates Gathered and Created a Disturbance

More Than Two Hundred People Surrounded the Inspection Office

The Office Staff Fled at the News

The Zhejiang Provincial Construction Department authorized an office to issue sand mining and transportation permits. Recently, an inspection office was set up on Wusong Wai Malu to collect sand and stone donations, with each ton costing seven jiao. A few days ago, dozens of sand and mud boats arrived at Wusongkou one after another. The director of the inspection office, Wang Bingheng, immediately sent personnel to board the boats on patrol ships to inspect them and order them to pay the donation according to the regulations. However, the sand and mud boats believed that this fee was similar to likin and refused to pay during the anti-likin period, causing an argument. The shipmates Dan Wencheng, Ying Agui, and seven others were detained ashore and held at the Seventh District Public Security Bureau. After hearing the news, the sand and mud boats were greatly indignant and gathered more than two hundred shipmates to rush to the inspection office at about 4:00 PM the day before yesterday. With great momentum, they immediately tore down the sign in front of the office and threw it away, declaring that they wanted to retrieve the detained shipmates. The office staff had already fled in advance at the news, so they were not beaten. Officer Li of the Seventh District Public Security Bureau led police to the scene to dissuade them, but because there were so many of them, there was no way to stop them for a while. Then, Shen Risheng, a standing committee member of the Eighth District Party Department, dissuaded them and notified the office to immediately release the seven shipmates held at the Public Security Bureau to avoid causing trouble. The shipmates then left in disappointment, and the storm subsided. The sand and mud boats have successively sailed into Shanghai yesterday to unload and sell their goods.

Policeman Shot and Injured a Woman on the Street While Chasing a Bicycle

The Policeman Claimed It Was an Accidental Injury

The Woman Suffered a Baseless Disaster

At 1:30 PM yesterday, a gunshot was heard near the intersection of Gonghe Road and Meiyuan Road in Zhabei. Police Officer Lü Rongxiang of the Sixth Precinct of the Second Section of the Fourth District thought it was a robbery and went towards the sound. He saw a woman lying on the ground with a gunshot wound, blood gushing from her right leg. At that time, there were two suspicious-looking people in front of him, running away frantically. The policeman desperately chased after them. Patrol Officers Gao Zhilin and Cao Jingui, who were in charge of the area and were distributing household registration forms, helped to apprehend the two people. They found a pistol on the spot, containing five bullets, and detained them together. The injured woman was sent to the hospital for treatment. Chief He interrogated the person in possession of the gun, who confessed that his name was Liu Yongxiang, from Baoshan, 30 years old, residing at No. 331 Datong Road. He was formerly a patrol officer of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau and had recently been supplemented to the detective team. The pistol belonged to Han Maosheng, a police officer in the Fourth District. Today, Han asked him to hide it for him because he had something to do. While passing by Meiyuan Road, a friend, Chen Amao (the other person arrested), was chasing after someone stealing a bicycle. He was helping him chase after the thief when the gun hidden in his waist suddenly fell to the ground, causing him to accidentally injure a pedestrian. He asked for leniency. He also presented his detective license from the Municipal Public Security Bureau for inspection. Chen's confession was similar to Liu's. Chief He then ordered the police to investigate the condition of the injured person in the hospital. It was found that the injured person was Zhang Jishi, from Yangzhou, 36 years old, residing at No. 2 Minli Road. She had a wound on her leg but was not in serious condition. She was bandaged and discharged from the hospital. Because the case involved a gunshot injury to a pedestrian, a report was prepared and submitted to the Judicial Section for review.

Everyone Was Busy Escaping

A Confusing and Perplexing Marital Lawsuit

Huan Longbao Accused of Abduction

His Father Invites a Matchmaker to Shanghai as Witness

Claiming It Was a Formal Wedding

Xu Binglong Firmly Denies It

Huan Longbao, son of a farmer from Meijiazhuang Village, Xinghua County, Jiangbei, and Zhao Di, the seventeen-year-old daughter of Xu Binglong, a farmer from Xiejiazhuang Village, Gaoyou County, a neighboring county, came to Shanghai last winter and resided at the home of their relative Sun Fulan at 235 Pingliang Road, Yangshupu, claiming to be husband and wife. Until last month, Xu Binglong suddenly reported to the local police that Huan and Sun had conspired to abduct his daughter and forcibly rape her. Zhao Di also denied having a marital relationship with Huan. The police then arrested Huan and Sun and brought them to the Special District Local Court. During the interrogation, Huan stated that Zhao Di was indeed his formally wedded wife, having married her in their hometown in August of last year, and that they subsequently came to Shanghai together. The judge ordered Huan and Sun to be detained pending the dispatch of letters to Xinghua and Gaoyou counties to investigate the matter. At this time, Xu Binglong received a letter from his elderly mother urging him to return home, so he took advantage of the official investigation period and hastily returned to his hometown. However, after arriving home, he learned the reason for his mother's summons: his wife had also been abducted by Huan Longbao's elder brother, known as "Little Hu," and had disappeared without a trace despite repeated searches. Unable to remain away from his duties in Shanghai for long, he had to leave his elderly mother alone at home. When he recently returned to Shanghai, the court had already received replies from Xinghua and Gaoyou counties. However, the information differed significantly. The Xinghua reply stated that Huan Longbao and Zhao Di were indeed formally husband and wife and included a marriage certificate. The Gaoyou reply stated that Xu Binglong's address could not be verified, and it was even more difficult to ascertain whether his daughter had been married to Huan. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao opened the court for a continued hearing. Huan Longbao's father, Huan Zhuping, specially invited the original matchmaker, Wang Yuzhang, to the court to testify. The judge first informed the plaintiff, Xu Binglong, of the contents of the Xinghua letter and presented the marriage certificate for his review. However, Xu still firmly denied ever agreeing to give his daughter in marriage to Huan's son. Zhao Di also echoed her father's statement. Subsequently, Huan Zhuping testified that he was seventy-five years old and had two sons, Little Hu and Longbao, both of whom had married. Longbao married Xu's daughter on August 16th of last year in their hometown. The matchmakers were Wang Yuzhang, Gao Yuemei, and Yao Sifa, and the total bride price was eighty yuan, paid in two installments. Later, on October 10th, his second son brought his daughter-in-law to Shanghai. This time, he had intended to invite all the matchmakers to court, but Gao and Yao were busy with farming and unable to leave. Only Wang Yuzhang was brought to testify. Wang stated that the two families lived only five or six miles apart and were well-acquainted. Therefore, they acted as matchmakers for the two families at that time, and everyone in the two villages knew about the wedding. How could it be a fabrication? The judge then inquired about the recent abduction of Xu Binglong's wife by Little Hu. Wang replied that he did not know about this. Thereupon, Xu testified that he had never met Wang Yuzhang and that his words were hardly believable. The marriage certificate attached by Xinghua County was also insufficient evidence, as it was obtained by county officials investigating the defendant's home and could have been copied from another marriage certificate by the defendant's family. He also retained lawyer Yuan Yang'an to state the reasons, saying that if Huan had married Xu's daughter as his wife, then it would be impossible for the legal wife to accuse her own husband of seduction and rape. Based on this point alone, it could be known that there was no marriage. The court believed that further investigation was necessary in this case and ordered the two defendants, Huan and Sun, to be remanded in custody, and the rest were dismissed to await investigation and further hearing.

Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities Bans Zangqiao Road Xiangyuan Lane Artesian Well

Supplying Residents Beyond Property Owners

And Urges Switching to Tap Water

The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities previously discovered that the artesian well set up by the owner, Taichang Company, in Xiangyuan Lane, 96 Zangqiao Road, Yinxiang District, also supplied residents of Hengxingfang and Dechang Lane on Zhangjiaxiang Road, violating the regulations of the city's Detailed Rules for Registration of Water Supply Equipment Self-Installed by Property Owners. Continued Hearing in the Huang Xianzhong Forged Check Case

Chen Zaifeng and Wang Zhiyuan Found Not Guilty

Chen Ziquan and Huang Xianzhong Released on Bail

The case of the Riye Bank was continued yesterday morning at the French Concession Court. Chen Zaifeng and Wang Zhiyuan of the Wanchun Silver Syndicate were present. Lawyer Peng Qi represented them, arguing that Huang Xianzhong had signed the checks on his own and that Chen Zaifeng and others had not induced him. The transfer of funds in Riye Bank did not harm the rights of Riye Bank, but it did cause losses to the Wanchun Silver Syndicate. Huang Xianzhong's defense lawyer, Tan Yigong, stated that the truth of Huang Xianzhong signing the checks was that Chen Ziquan came on January 18th to request Huang Chu-jiu to countersign the checks to complete the transfer procedure, which Huang Chu-jiu agreed to. On the 19th, Chen came again to request the countersigning. Huang Chu-jiu, being seriously ill and unable to hold a pen, ordered Huang Xianzhong to sign on his behalf and handed it to Chen Ziquan to take away. Chen Zaifeng, Wang Zhiyuan, and others were all present at the scene. Huang Xianzhong signed on behalf of his father at the request of Chen Ziquan, the manager of Riye Bank, with his father's consent, merely to complete the transfer procedure. He did not withdraw any cash and did not gain any benefit from it. It did not cause any damage to Riye Bank. The funds transferred to Wanchun were still designated for payment to Riye Bank and were not used for his own purposes. Therefore, this act of signing on behalf of his father with the consent of all parties should not be considered a crime. He requested that the case be dismissed. The accountant requested a strict investigation of Chen Ziquan's alteration and destruction of accounting books. Judge Zhu adjourned the hearing due to the lateness of the hour and ordered a rescheduling. Chen Zaifeng and Wang Zhiyuan were found not guilty. Chen Ziquan, Huang Xianzhong, and others remained released on bail. The defense statement of Huang Xianzhong is recorded as follows:

Regarding the case of Shanghai Riye Bank's fraudulent transfer of funds, I hereby submit a defense and request that it be verified and pronounced innocent. The financial dealings between Shanghai Riye Bank and my family were always managed by my late father, Huang Chu-jiu. I never handled them personally. Regarding the five checks issued on January 19th of this year, totaling over one million yuan, it is true that I signed those checks when my late father was terminally ill, on the day of his death. Chen Ziquan, the manager of Riye Bank, and others brought a new checkbook to my home and requested my late father to consent to sign the above checks to complete the transfer procedure. At that time, my late father was severely ill and unable to sign personally. He ordered me to sign on his behalf. Chen Ziquan and others declared to me that this was to complete the already transferred procedure and did not involve withdrawing cash, and that there were no conflicts of interest. They urged me to sign and hand it over to Chen Ziquan for safekeeping. When my father was on the verge of death, I was overwhelmed with grief and pain. I could not choose between the existence of the transfer of interests, and the appropriateness of signing on behalf of the check, especially by the order of my father, what choice can I make in a hurry? And many of the people at the scene were my father's friends, and they all said it was a legitimate procedure. Therefore, I followed the consensus and signed the checks on behalf of my father, purely out of passivity, and not autonomously. At the time of signing on behalf of my father, I had no intention of greedily obtaining improper benefits, nor did I have the intention of harming the interests of others. Now, I would like to separately clarify the important points of the trial regarding my part, namely (1) the act of signing on behalf of my father, and (2) the transfer caused the debt with mortgage rights of Riye Bank to become a debt without mortgage rights, as follows: (1) The checks signed by me on behalf of my father were because the manager Chen Ziquan, after the transfer, requested my late father to agree and issue checks to complete the transfer procedure, and it was not that I used the checks to withdraw cash from the bank. This has been recognized as a fact in this case. What should be studied is whether my act of following my father's order to sign these checks on his behalf constitutes a crime. The act of payment stated on the check was originally the right and obligation of my late father. I was originally the heir to that right and obligation. A son signing on behalf of his father is different from the act of signing a check on behalf of others. Moreover, at the time of signing on behalf of my father, Chen Ziquan, the manager of Riye Bank, and others requested my late father to agree and ordered me to sign on his behalf, which is even less comparable to a private forgery. There is no formal provision in criminal law that recognizes it as constituting a crime. Even if the issuance of this check hinders the rights and obligations of others, it is, at most, an invalid act in civil law, and cannot involve the scope of criminal detention, let alone be compared with the act of forging, altering, or destroying accounting books. The matter is very clear. (2) The transfer of funds in Riye Bank had already been transferred by Manager Chen Ziquan with my late father's consent before I signed the checks on his behalf. The propriety of the transfer does not involve me, so there is no need to argue about it. However, the accountant's accusation is that the transfer caused the debt with mortgage rights of Riye Bank to become a debt without mortgage rights, which damaged the interests of Riye Bank and its creditors. The mortgaged goods (i.e., property deeds, etc.) were originally owned by my late father and were handed over to Riye Bank for mortgage to Siming and China Industrial Bank to obtain banknotes of 800,000 yuan. Later, due to the financial difficulties of Riye Bank, my late father, during his lifetime, transferred the aforementioned mortgaged goods, together with additional mortgaged goods, to Wanchun Silver Syndicate for a loan of 300,000 yuan, all of which was agreed to be fully allocated to Riye Bank to repay the debt. It is different from the situation of transferring the cash for personal use or for other purposes. Therefore, this kind of behavior does not actually harm the interests of Riye Bank itself and its creditors at all. As for the account allocation and payment of the mortgage amount by Wanchun Silver Syndicate, it is a breach of contract by Wanchun Silver Syndicate. My late father and I should not bear any responsibility. Moreover, all the inheritance of my late father has been handed over to repay the debt in full. There is no intention of benefiting myself and harming others. There is no such thing as making a debt with mortgage rights into a debt without mortgage rights. Furthermore, considering that the accountant who exercised the right to accuse in this case did not consider the act of me signing on behalf of my father to be a crime or add an accusation, it is sufficient to show that the behavior related to me does not constitute a crime and is not doubtful. Based on the above reasons, I humbly request that the court carefully examine the part of this case where I signed the check on behalf of my father, and pronounce me innocent. This would be fair and convenient. Submitted to the Shanghai French Concession Court for public inspection on May 14th, 20th year of the Republic of China. Petitioner Huang Xianzhong, Defense Lawyer Tan Yigong.

Sentenced to Ten Days of Detention

Shi believed that foreigners bullying Chinese people had become a habit, and if there was no serious negotiation, it would be unimaginable in the future. Summary of Housing Disputes

Guangxing Lane: The tenant association of the Wulifang building on Peng Road held an emergency joint meeting of all executive supervisors at the association at 2:00 PM yesterday because the landlord had not withdrawn the order to increase the rent after two letters of request. More than 50 people attended, chaired by Tang Huilian. After the formalities were completed, the chairman announced the landlord's second reply and then discussed the following: (1) The plan to actively prepare for countermeasures was divided into four methods: (A) Ask legal counsel to be responsible for negotiations. (B) Ask the Shanghai Special District Citizens Association and the Hongkou Tenant General Association to provide impartial assistance. (C) During the unresolved time, all rents will be paid according to the original amount. If the landlord does not accept it, it will be properly deposited in Wing On Bank, and the association will issue a notice to all tenants. (D) According to the order issued by the Nanjing National Government, Shanghai Municipal Government, and Shanghai Municipal Council on June 27, 1927, landlords must not increase rents without reason, and tenants must not reduce rents on the pretext. Should we submit a request to ban the landlord's disregard for the authorities' orders this time? It was decided to submit a jointly signed request to achieve the goal. (2) The economic issue was decided to be discussed next time, but all current miscellaneous expenses should be temporarily advanced by the economic section. (3) Should we publish a statement denying the case? It was decided to have a legal advisor represent the denial. (4) Other proposals. The meeting did not end until after 7:00 PM.

Tongxing Lane: The housing dispute in Tongxing Lane on Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession has lasted for many days. The landlord sent dozens of Russians to demolish the house the day before yesterday. The tenants came forward to stop them, but due to language barriers, a misunderstanding arose and a conflict occurred. The Russian leader directed all the Russians to use force. The tenants, unable to resist, immediately called the police for help. One Russian leader, in his haste to chase the tenants, tripped and fell on the side of the street, hitting his head and bleeding. Those who were watching on the road laughed at him. The Russian became even more ashamed and angry, and grabbed someone walking on the road, pointing to him as the one who beat him. The police arrived and took the man and the Russian to the Big Ben Police Station together. Then, the police sent someone to summon the tenants to the writing room to inquire about the truth. After the tenant representatives explained the situation, the police rebuked the Russians and ordered them not to do such things again in the future. However, the man on the road was designated by the Russian as the one who caused him to fall, and was detained by the police for several hours.

Baoan Lane: Regarding the rent dispute in Baoan Lane on Avenue Joffre in the French Concession, here is the company's reply to the tenants: We are replying to your letter. We have learned everything. Since our company purchased the houses in Baoan Lane, the relationship with the tenants has been extremely harmonious. However, since last year, the tenants have repeatedly requested repairs, and some have said that the company should be responsible for any dangers. Some have also proposed to deduct the repair costs from the rent. Our company has repeatedly sent people to estimate the cost of repairs, which is about 200 taels of land for each building. If calculated based on rent, the loss will be as much as one year. Our company, in order to respect the tenants, cannot but agree to repair, but the loss is too great, and there is hesitation in proceeding. Therefore, although the notice was limited to May 5th, work has not yet started. Now that the executive directors have formally requested a postponement of repairs on behalf of the tenants, our company may not disagree, but it is hoped that the following two conditions can be implemented before we can proceed: (1) All rent arrears must be paid in full, with written proof that no claims will be made against our company for disrepair in the future. This most legitimate and minimum requirement, I believe your representatives must have the right to handle. Your representatives must know that the property belongs to the landlord, and all dispositions have special privileges, which cannot be demanded by the tenants. This time, for the sake of harmonious relations, we are making a special step. I hope you will understand. If the above two conditions cannot be fulfilled, then our company will have to take appropriate actions based on the law of ownership. Is it feasible? Please reply.

Tram Company Mechanics Demand Bail for Fellow Workers

The mechanics of the Public Concession Tram Company's factory went on strike on the morning of the 14th to demand the release of arrested workers. The mechanics from the factories on Bubbling Well Road, Hart Road, and Yangtzepoo Road, totaling about 500 people, joined the strike, demanding the release of Qiao Shengfa, a worker who was arrested by the police station on May 11th. However, the workers still went to work as usual the day before yesterday. It was not until around 3:00 PM that the mechanics in the factories on Bubbling Well Road and other roads announced a slowdown. The company immediately reported to the police station and ordered detectives to be stationed at the entrances of the copper shops on Bubbling Well Road and Hart Road as a precaution. The workers then sent representatives to contact the company, still using the bail of Qiao Shengfa as a condition for resuming work. The company replied that the company and the Concession Police Station are both foreign and have a good relationship, and have nothing to do with the Public Security Bureau. If Qiao is detained at the police station, we can try to help, but it is really difficult to approve of the fact that he is now detained at the Public Security Bureau. It is not intentionally making things difficult, but it is a factual impossibility. The coppersmiths once wanted to contact the ticket sellers and drivers to go on strike together, but they did not achieve their goal. Now, some workers understand the company's difficulties and are quite hopeful of returning to their old ways, so the labor tide will not expand and there may be hope for a peaceful resolution.

The Problem of Training Management Talent

Xu Peihuang's Speech at the Industrial and Commercial Management Association

The Chinese Industrial and Commercial Management Association held its eighth luncheon discussion meeting yesterday afternoon at the United Chinese Association. They invited Mr. Xu Peihuang, Director of the Municipal Education Bureau, to give a speech entitled "The Problem of Training Management Talent." Those present included Xu Peihuang, Guo Bingwen, Fang Jiaobo, Li Zhaoshuai, Shou Jingwei, Wu Qingtai, Chen Da, Wu Yun Chu, Li Zufan, He Qingru, Tao Leqin, Cao Yunxiang, Pan Wenan, Gu Xun, Wu Kejia, Ji Jiannan, Zhu Yinjiang, Chen En'yi, Chen Wan Yun, Zhao Shutong, Kong Shi'e, Shi Jiuyun, Liu Musu, Zhang Ziyuan, Li Yunliang, Shen Junsheng, Le Yuanzhang, Huang Zhongming, Chang Bicheng, Xu Chao, etc. Dr. Kong Yongzhi, the chairman, was absent due to official business. Member Shou Jingwei was temporarily elected as chairman. After the meal, the chairman delivered the opening remarks, followed by Mr. Xu Peihuang's speech, which mainly emphasized that during training, attention should be paid to aspects such as thought, initiative, morality, responsibility, duty, etiquette, obedience, and punctuality. Although China has many talented individuals, their sense of responsibility seems somewhat weak. If everyone is willing to take responsibility, there will be significant benefits to both the economy and time, and so on. Subsequently, Mr. Pan Wenan proposed that the training of management talent is indeed very important, and suggested whether the Industrial and Commercial Management Association, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and the Bankers' Association could jointly organize a training institute for management personnel. After discussion, Pan Wenan, He Qingru, and Cao Yunxiang were publicly elected to draft the organizational outline and solicit opinions from all parties. If there is unanimous agreement, they will then discuss joint measures with the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Bankers' Association. The meeting adjourned at 2:15 PM.

Dismissal of Navigation Staff of the Inland Rivers Merchant Bureau

The Inland Rivers Merchant Bureau was leased by the Zhejiang Provincial Government in June of last year to revitalize inland river navigation. Chen Shuntong, Zhang Yangsheng, and Sheng Qunian were appointed to be in charge, under the jurisdiction of the Department of Construction. After painstaking management, some success was achieved. However, with the reorganization of the provincial government and Shi Ying succeeding as the Director of the Zhejiang Department of Construction, due to financial constraints in Zhejiang Province, austerity measures were implemented, reducing the operating expenses for construction projects by more than eight million yuan annually. The Inland Rivers Merchant Bureau also dispatched Shi Zhaoji to Shanghai to reorganize. After taking office, Shi began to wind down operations, gradually leasing out all shipping routes. The main routes of the Shanghai Bureau, such as the Shenhu Line, the Shensu Line, and the Shenhang Line, were also leased out by Shi Zhaoji after meetings with various shipping merchants. After many days of negotiations, these three routes have now been completely leased to merchants. The Shenhu Line was leased to the Lixing Company, the Shensu Line was leased by no one, and the Shenhang Line was leased to Dai Shengchang. As of yesterday, the three main routes were completely handed over to the leaseholders. The Inland Rivers Bureau has leased out all twenty-one routes and no longer operates any ships itself. At the same time, the business office of the Shanghai Inland Rivers Steamboat Company was also closed, and all navigation department staff, totaling more than twenty people, were dismissed yesterday. Their salaries for this month were paid, and they were immediately ordered to leave the bureau. A management office was established in Shanghai, its business limited to collecting rent. Other staff, such as customs brokers and warehouse staff, were also dismissed. The office now has only six people. It has been exactly one year since Zhang Jingjiang leased the bureau last year, and the grand plan to revitalize inland navigation has now been fundamentally abandoned.

Steamboat Smuggling Cases

Military Supplies: The French cargo ship "Yulu," which arrived in Shanghai from Marseille, Europe, entered the port at 4:00 PM the day before yesterday. Customs officers boarded the ship for inspection and found twenty-three smuggled handguns, each with one hundred rounds of ammunition, totaling 2,300 rounds, in the ship's coal bunker. The customs officers seized the guns and ammunition and confiscated them, while investigating the smugglers for prosecution.

Grain: The Chinese steamship "Daxing" left Shanghai for Vladivostok yesterday. Upon leaving Shanghai, eighty-five bags of smuggled white rice were discovered. The customs authorities, noting that it had not been reported, considered it to be smuggled for export and immediately seized it. A barge was dispatched to seize the rice and unload it into the customs warehouse, pending discussion of penalties.

Concrete Measures to Ban Japanese Fishing Vessels

Approved by the Seamen's Union

The Chinese Seamen's Industrial Federation sent a notice yesterday to its various branches stating that the Central Training Department of the Chinese Nationalist Party issued Order No. 15136, stating: "Previously, this association reported that Japanese fishing vessels were using Chinese traitors to hoist our national flag and plunder marine products, requesting review and instructions for prompt handling. This matter was reported to the National Government Secretariat and submitted for review. Now, a reply has been received stating: 'Greetings, Your Department's letter No. 14842 regarding the Chinese Seamen's Union Federation Organizing Committee's report that Japanese fishing vessels are using Chinese traitors to hoist our national flag and plunder marine products, requesting transfer for prompt handling, has been received and acknowledged. This matter was submitted to the National Government for approval, stating the investigation and reply. Regarding the protection of fisheries, the Executive Yuan previously submitted a proposal from the Ministry of Industry, which was reviewed by the Ministries of Finance, Industry, and Navy, and then reported back. This was then submitted to the 17th State Council meeting for resolution, instructing the relevant ministries to properly plan for protection and requesting the National Government to exempt fishing taxes and fishery taxes, which the government has already ordered to be uniformly exempted. Subsequently, Shi Renhang, Zhuang Songfu, and the Jiangsu Provincial Government telegraphed that Japanese fishing vessels were invading our territorial waters, requesting the dispatch of warships for protection. These matters were all submitted to the Executive Yuan and approved for reply, and were also submitted to the 21st State Council meeting for resolution, in accordance with the review opinions of the Ministries of Industry, Finance, and Navy at the 17th State Council meeting. However, the leasing of vessels should be changed to having the Navy dispatch two warships to patrol and protect, and the Ministries of Industry, Finance, and Navy should still promptly formulate an overall plan to effectively handle the matter. Now, approval has been granted based on the previous reasons, and the related investigation report is enclosed for reference.' The original investigation report is enclosed. This is to inform the association, and a copy of the original investigation report is enclosed with this order for the association's information. This order is issued to all departments, and a copy of the attachment is sent with this document for the association's information. This order is issued on the fifth month of the twentieth year of the Republic of China, by Chairman Zhao Zhizhi, Committee Members Lin Yinsheng, Liang Degong, Huang Yushu, and Miao Shuizhang."

Wang Yinfu Implicated in the Ningbo Opium Case

Wang Yinfu, an accountant from Cixi at the Yuanyu Silver Shop in Pentang Lane, secretly purchased opium from Shanghai, mixed it with other goods, and shipped it to Ningbo for sale by steamboat. He also contacted the local opium dealer Mao Aru in Ningbo. When the opium arrived, he would retrieve it. Recently, the matter was exposed, and Mao was arrested by the Yinxian police. During interrogation by the local court, Mao confessed that Wang was the mastermind. Because Wang was practicing in Shanghai and had repeatedly failed to appear when summoned, the court prepared an official letter and sent judicial police to Shanghai to request the assistance of the Shanghai Special District Court's police to arrest and bring him to court for trial. Yesterday, the police arrested Wang and sent him to the Special Court, while Wang hired lawyer Wu Linkun to defend him, stating that the defendant was a respectable merchant and that this matter was likely a false accusation. He requested permission for the defendant to be released on bail and go to the Ningbo court to confront the accusers in person, to avoid immediate deportation. Judge Zhou immediately granted the request, ordering Wang Yinfu to post a bond of one thousand yuan and go to the Qin County Court within one week to await interrogation.

Opium Hidden in Duck Eggshells

Chen Shoumei's Wild Dreams

Chinese Police Crack Down on Cracked Preserved Eggs

Chen Shoumei, from Anhui, works as a tea room attendant on Yangtze River steamboats and usually smuggles opium. Recently, due to strict crackdowns, he hollowed out duck eggs, hid two taels of opium inside the eggshells, and covered them with mud and bran, making them look like preserved eggs. He has smuggled them more than once. At 8:00 AM the day before yesterday, Chen was carrying a bamboo basket containing more than twenty of these preserved eggs, and was walking on Yade Road when he was spotted by Chinese police officer No. 1243 at the third intersection. Suspecting him, they searched him and broke the preserved eggs, finding that twelve of them contained opium, weighing a total of twenty-four taels. They arrested Chen and seized the opium, taking them to the police station to await investigation.

The China Crown Life Insurance Company Established

The Crown Life Insurance Co. was founded in 1900 in Toronto, Canada. The chairman is Mr. Bolton, who served as the Prime Minister of Canada during the European War and as the chief representative of Canada in the International League of Nations. He is currently the chairman of Barclays Bank. Other directors are also leading industrialists in Canada. The general manager is Stephenson, the vice president of the American Life Insurance Association. It has strong assets and a good reputation. As of last year, its assets were valued at 160 million US dollars. It has many business characteristics, the most notable of which are: (1) It uses the latest life expectancy tables, and its premiums are 9 to 14 percent lower than those of ordinary life insurance institutions; (2) It can provide the highest amount of coverage; (3) It is closely supervised by the Canadian government. Recently, in order to promote business in China and Hong Kong, it has established the China Crown Company at No. 1 Jiujiang Road in Shanghai.

After much selection and careful consideration, they chose Jin Liansheng, a 25-year-old from Jiading who works at the Hong Kong Laundry Company on Yuyuan Road. All his qualifications meet the association's matchmaking regulations, and both parties expressed satisfaction. The Public Security Bureau also sent personnel to investigate and approve. The wedding was held yesterday at the association's orphanage in Zhabei. Representatives from the Social Affairs Bureau and the Public Security Bureau also attended the ceremony. All the executive members of the association, as well as the members of the education department and all the staff, were present at the ceremony. The attire was formal and the ceremony was solemn.

Free Talk

World Anecdotes

—Hai Ke

A lecturer at Cambridge University in England is planning to build a modern house. The doors and walls are made entirely of glass. The woodwork is made of metal and glass. There is also a fountain with colored lights at night, which is very gorgeous.

The most fashionable women in Europe and America often spend a lot of money on decoration. Hairdressing alone can cost up to 500 pounds a year, which is about 20,000 yuan in Mexican silver. The average hairdressing fee for ordinary women is 8 pounds per person per year.

Sir S. Cobham, an English aviator, flew all over England in 1929. His plane carried 40,000 passengers and flew 60,000 miles without stopping.

In New York's major commercial organizations, employees taking sick leave due to colds has caused work to be delayed and affected business. Statistics show that this loss exceeds 1 million pounds per year.

According to a British medical scientist, if we can pay attention to our daily life and avoid catching colds, we can add five years to our life expectancy.

Extravagant Tales from American Prohibition

—Zheng Yimei

It is said that alcohol makes one immoral and weakens the nerves, because its numbing effect is very strong. The American ban on alcohol is very strict, and the fines are heavier than in other countries. Ordinary drinkers are not allowed to gather and drink heartily, which makes them very depressed. They hide a bottle of wine in the bottom of a boat during their weekends and sail to a place where the waves are vast and there are no traces of people. Then they sing wildly and drink freely, enjoying themselves all day long. But the hidden bottle of wine is discovered by the police after a long time, and the drinkers are arrested and get to experience the taste of jail. The timid dare not defy the law and buy Burmese wine tree fruit to eat, just to comfort themselves. The fruit of the wine tree is shaped like a coconut. When it is opened, the juice is white and sweet, with a slight taste of wine. Drinking too much can also make people drunk. However, it is expensive and difficult to buy. Then, they come up with a strange idea and make wine into dry powder, which is transported by women. They pretend to have their monthly period and cleverly hide the dry wine in their menstrual belts to avoid the eyes of the police. When it arrives, they mix it with water and it becomes fine wine. The anecdotes of banning alcohol are even more bizarre than the smuggling of opium in our country during the ban on opium. It is said that a rich man in New York, Lu Lixu, is so rich that he can do anything. He bought 10,000 jars of wine and poured them all into the pool. One day, he hosted a banquet for guests and had young women swim naked in the wine pool. The jade bodies were beautiful, and the wine was even more fragrant. The guests indulged themselves without restraint. When the wine was empty, the naked women scooped wine from the pool and filled it until the pool was dry. The naked women then got up and danced, the wine fragrance spreading and the spring scenery was full of vitality. His extravagance was unprecedented and outrageous. A friend who has lived in America for many years told me about this. He is also a drinker and said that getting wine in America is almost like getting jade nectar.

Chaste Woman from a Brothel

—Zui Chi Sheng

How can there be a chaste woman from a brothel? How can a chaste woman be in a brothel? But such a thing actually happened, which is also strange. According to the author, I once wrote an article entitled "The Poor Bride," which was published in this column. It recorded that Miss Lu from the neighbor's family guarded her chastity and married a dead person. The protagonist in this article is Miss Lu. After the woman swore to guard her chastity, she spent her lonely years. Time passed quickly, and three years passed in a flash. The woman's strange encounters were beyond her expectations and beyond her ability to bear. At first, the woman wept and married Mr. So-and-so. It was out of a sincere enthusiasm that she put everything aside, not to gain anything. The woman's mother-in-law got this unexpected woman and treated her very well on weekdays. All the food, clothing, and utensils were provided. And she was considerate and thoughtful. When she went out, she provided a car to travel, and when she entered, she had a record player to please her ears. But the mother-in-law's plan was actually very hopeful for the woman. The mother-in-law was a procuress and ran a brothel in Beili. The woman's residence was close to the brothel, so she could be influenced by what she saw and heard and gradually become a member of the brothel. But the woman accidentally entered the drunken and dreamy place and saw the charming and enchanting gestures of the women. She covered her face and ran away, ashamed to be with them. The woman guarded her body like jade and was not moved by the environment. Her mother-in-law was very angry when she got this stubborn woman. From then on, the relationship between the mother-in-law and daughter-in-law was like fire and water. In the winter of last year, the mother-in-law had no choice but to force the woman to move into the brothel, saying that since the woman came, the expenses had increased day by day and she had to take austerity measures to reduce expenses. The woman heard this and sobbed all night, saying that she would rather die than be a flower in a dirty place. The next day, she told her mother-in-law that she was going back to her hometown. When she left, the mother-in-law said sternly, "It's good that you're going back. Are there few people here who can eat your rice? But all the clothes and jewelry are owned by our family and you can't take them." Although the woman was reluctant, she had no choice. Now the woman has been back for several months. I have seen her cut her hair short and wear leather shoes, dressed in the latest fashion, but her face shows dimples and her charm is still there. The woman is still a pure and innocent girl. But she suddenly became a bride, suddenly became a chaste woman, and almost became a prostitute who sold her smiles. Now she has returned with broken wings. (She cannot live in peace and guard her chastity.) She has returned to her girlhood life. Her life has been extremely volatile and unpredictable. I don't know what her heart feels. But her father is confused and has not completely broken off with Mr. So-and-so. He has not sought a marriage partner for her, and he is also tight-lipped about it. There is no intention to seek a phoenix.

The Train Waits for People

—Ying Dai

When we go out traveling, we have to catch the train. We must follow the train schedule at the station, otherwise, if we are late by one minute, or even one second, the train will not wait for you for a moment. However, there is also a case where the train waits for people. Isn't that strange? It turns out that in Hyderabad, India, there is a man named Nizam. He is the richest man in the world. His family's property totals 200 billion US dollars. Behind his residence, there is a station with a private train parked there. Every day, it is always on fire as if it is about to leave. That is the case even if he does not want to go out. Someone asked him, and he said, "Should the train wait for people? Or should people wait for the train?" This way, whenever he wants to go out traveling, the train will start immediately and he doesn't have to wait.

A Record of a Visit to Jin Xian Temple

— Chen Boying

Jin Xian Temple is the largest Buddhist temple in the Cixi County area. It was first built in the Ming Dynasty, to the west of Minghe field, on the shores of Baiyang Lake. The scenery is quite beautiful. Recently, I visited a friend in Cixi and took the opportunity to visit it. The temple faces south, backed by mountains and facing the lake. Built along the mountain, its atmosphere is imposing. In front is the mountain gate, leading to the Hall of the Heavenly Kings, where the Four Heavenly Kings are enshrined, representing favorable wind, seasonable weather, peace and abundant harvest. The statues are about twenty feet tall. Further in is the Grand Hall of the Great Hero, enshrining the Tathagata. The hall is deep and profound. A Buddhist ceremony was being performed at the time, with about twenty or thirty monks. The sounds of bells and chimes were melodious, and the smoke of incense swirled around. The sound of the chanting rose slowly, giving one the desire to transcend the world. Behind the hall stands the Great Merciful Guanyin Bodhisattva, standing upright. Further in is the Abbot's room, on the wall of which hangs a Buddhist painting by Bailongshan Ren, with a vivid spirit. I sipped tea here. The temple was rebuilt during the Guangxu era, so the beams and pillars still look new. Beside the hall are dozens of guest rooms, dining halls, and monks' quarters, interspersed with pines and cypresses. There are several dozen monks who chant sutras. Initially, residents often saw a golden-robed monk with a staff standing halfway up the mountain on moonlit nights. The bolder ones approached to look closely, but there was nothing there. They then knew it was a manifestation of the Buddha, and they raised money to build the temple. That is how it got its name. The mountain behind the temple is called Beiling Peak. The whole mountain is planted with pines, and the tombs are piled up, giving a sense of Beimang. Climbing to the top, Baiyang Lake is right at your feet, surrounded by mountains like a water basin. Reeds grow densely in the lake. The white water and green reeds reflect each other in exceptional beauty. Small boats drift leisurely, and water birds emerge and disappear, enough to be in a painting. The lake covers two hundred acres, fed by streams and valleys, so it is vast and seems boundless. Gazing at it, I don't know how many bushels of worldly dust were swept away. After descending, I returned along the embankment. A gentle breeze blew, stirring the water into roaring sounds, as if seeing me off. We live in the city every day, and the dust clogs our mouths and noses, making us want to choke. Compared to the fishermen, woodcutters, and shepherds who enjoy the mountain scenery and feast on the lake's beauty, what are their gains and losses? What are their gains and losses? Written after returning from Jin Xian Temple.

A Clean Freak

— Shi Yan Ye

Cleanliness is a virtue. However, too much of a good thing is as bad as too little. Not only will one not be loved and respected, but one will also incur resentment. Let me describe two cases to aid in conversation.

In Zhabei, there is a certain Mr. A who is a clean freak. He lives in a standalone house, and the rooms are exceptionally clean. The windows are bright and the tables are spotless, not a speck of dust to be seen. Even the floor is scrubbed daily, surpassing even the cleanliness of the Japanese tatami mats. The stairs leading to the upper floor, because the steps touch his clothes, are constantly swept and brushed. Servants who are even slightly negligent are immediately scolded. Even the slightest speck of dirt will result in scolding, and no one in the household is spared. He also practices sweeping only the snow in front of his own door outside, instructing the servants to sweep the dirt to both sides and wash it with clean water three or four times a day. Both the front and back doors are the same. Compared to the neighbors, one is dirty and one is clean, a natural divide. Anyone entering the neighborhood who does not know his residence can identify it by the cleanliness of its doorway. Guests all regard him as a source of fear, and only visit when absolutely necessary. When they do visit, they must first check their shoes and brush their clothes before entering. Once inside, they must not touch anything and must be careful not to cough or spit. The ashes from their cigarettes must not fall to the ground. Otherwise, even if he does not explicitly order them to leave, his face will show his displeasure. Therefore, he has very little interaction with others, and even his servants cannot stay with him for long.

Formerly, in a certain school, there was a colleague, a certain Mr. B, who was also exceptionally fond of cleanliness. Every morning, he would take his bedding to the sports ground, pat it, and wipe it before folding it up and hanging his mosquito net to prevent dust from entering. He would not rely on the school workers to clean his chairs and tables. After washing up, he would use the remaining water to wet a towel and wipe them, from the surface of the desks and chairs to all four legs, repeatedly. He kept a kettle for his drinks and would wash it himself every morning. After wiping the outside, he would also clean the inside, filling it with clear spring water, pouring it out and refilling it, at least ten times. No one was allowed to touch his bed, desk, or any of his belongings. Anyone who did would incur his anger. If he went home, every piece of paper and every pen would be placed in a specific location. If anyone moved them, he would immediately know and would verbally abuse them. Therefore, his colleagues all kept their distance from him. I was with him for a year and spoke to him less than ten times.

Travelogue Around the Yellow Sea (5)

— Huang Yanpei

Japan is beset everywhere by economic recession. This can be seen from the city of Dalian. The public trams have not been oiled for a long time. The street signs are peeling and difficult to read. Under Japanese administration in normal times, this would not happen. Once you get to Shenyang, it is very different. Although the economy is said to be bad, in Shenyang city, it is hard to find a decent hotel to accommodate three or four people, even with the efforts of many people for a whole day. It seems that the qualified hotels are all fully booked. But locals tell me that the majority of travelers in Shenyang city are there for political reasons.

I haven't been to Shenyang for four years. In these four years, many new markets have been opened, and many new streets and houses have indeed been added. It is said that last year, gold prices soared and soybeans were difficult to sell, which indeed had a very negative impact. But the previous few years were very good. Every time a new avenue was built, it would be filled with shops and residents in less than a year. I heard that the Shenyang municipal authorities are very talented and courageous.

The two points I pay special attention to are: (1) Future international predictions. (2) The current social and economic situation.

North Manchuria and Soviet Russia, South Manchuria and Japan, all kinds of international disputes are centered on the railway. To remove the shackles, it is necessary to open up an outlet from the transportation. This is only natural. In these few years, the government of Dong Province has actually completed the construction of the railways east and west of the South Manchurian Railway in complete silence. Some were borrowed money, and some used their own money. No wonder the Japanese were shocked. The Tanaka Memorial said, "Little attention was paid beforehand. Afterwards, when we tried to forcibly stop it, the railway line had already been completed." —

Map of the New Railway Lines to the Left and Right of the South Manchurian Railway

The Hawthorne Detective Agency Turns a Corner (16)

— Cheng Xiaoqing

Hawthorne's suggestion to investigate in the Gao family’s direction was certainly considerate. However, he only told me to go to Pei Fen to inquire. For a moment, I was somewhat suspicious. Could he be suspecting that this person had some relationship with Pei Fen? Someone as young and innocent as Pei Fen would hardly be associated with such a conspirator. Hawthorne's nerves seemed rather sensitive. But since he had decided on a course of action, I did not dare change it without authorization. The next morning, Pei Qin's condition showed slight improvement. Her fever had subsided, which relieved me somewhat. After breakfast, I hurried to the Gao residence. The opportunity was good this time. My parents-in-law had been busy with social engagements the previous night and felt tired, so they had not yet gotten up. Pei Xian, however, had gone to the Garrison Headquarters early in the morning. When I entered, the maid, Xiao Mei, told me that Miss Pei Fen had gotten up not long ago and was getting dressed upstairs. I asked Xiao Mei to go upstairs and announce me and waited in the study downstairs. After waiting for about ten minutes, I heard the sound of leather shoes clicking as she walked quickly into the study. She was wearing a pure black, fine swastika-patterned moonflower gauze qipao, which reached her ankles. Her lively eyes smiled as she approached me to greet me. She said, "Brother-in-law, you're here so early. My brother said that you escaped from the banquet last night without saying goodbye. He's going to talk to you about it today." I replied, "Last night, I was worried about your sister, who had a bit of a fever, and I was afraid of being trapped by the other guests and forced to drink, so I quietly went home. Today, I was planning to come and apologize." The smile on Pei Fen's face immediately disappeared. She quickly asked, "How is my sister? Does she still have a fever?" I said, "Her fever has subsided this morning, so she should be fine." As I said this, I got to the point and planned to start my mission of inquiry. However, I didn't know how to bring it up. Pei Fen seemed to have seen through my intentions. She suddenly asked, "Since that's the case, why does your face still look so worried?" I took the opportunity to say, "Last night, I encountered a strange thing. Someone seemed to want to harm me." Her eyes flickered for a moment. She suddenly clapped her slender hands and said, "Oh, brother-in-law, have you brought another strange case? Tell me, tell me. I haven't heard a strange story for a long time." I said seriously, "Today, I'm not here to tell you a story, but to have you tell me one." Pei Fen's gaze rested on my face for a moment. She seemed to realize that I was not joking, so she suppressed her smile. She asked, "What? How can I tell a story?" I said, "Not a story. I want you to identify someone." So I described the appearance and clothing of the person I met last night to Pei Fen, asking if she recognized him.

Delayed Development of American Cotton

Market Conditions Softened Due to Securities

New York, 15th: A report on the raw cotton market conditions during the week stated that the cotton market fell due to soft securities market conditions and favorable weather in the cotton-growing areas. The delayed development of cotton crops and seeds remains an important issue. However, with proper soil preparation, progress can proceed smoothly. According to an expert, approximately 65% of the cotton fields have been sown, compared to 75% at the same time last year. The reduction in cotton field planting is between 8% and 12%. Recent rains have delayed the start of cotton cultivation, but they have been beneficial to the soil. Sentiment remains bearish, but sellers have decreased because prices are too low and the future of the new crop is still uncertain.

Flour Market Booming

Rumors of Government Imposing Export Tax

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning and afternoon, the prices of all months rebounded strongly. The telegrams about the Yangfen wheat incident the day before had not been answered as of yesterday, causing the sentiment of inland merchants to reignite. They eagerly absorbed positions in both near and distant months. Although the current flour sales market did not appear particularly robust, the attitude of major factories was not as inclined to dump inventory as before. Sometimes they were even seen buying, which made inland merchants feel more secure. In the afternoon trading sessions, there were even rumors that the government would impose an export tax, further stimulating buying activity. However, demand from Tianjin merchants remained weak, suggesting that ordering foreign flour may be unavoidable in the future. As a result, the current month rose by 1.5 points compared to the previous day, June rose by 1.75 points, July rose by 1.5 points, August rose by 1 point, and September and October rose by 2 points.

Strong Buying Interest in Wheat Futures

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat futures market in the morning and afternoon, the prices of all months generally showed a positive trend. The sentiment of inland merchants shifted because the new wheat crop this year was generally inferior to previous years, and because it was difficult to continue ordering foreign wheat due to unfavorable cost. Future demand will inevitably rely more on new wheat, so sentiment shifted, and buying interest increased significantly. Given this situation, it may be difficult to see prices fall in the future. As a result, the current month was up 5 points compared to the previous day, June was up 5 points, July was up 4 points, August was up 5 points, September was up 4 points, and October was up 3 points.

Silk, Tea, and Foreign Firms: The Silk Market Is Becoming Clearer

Overseas silk sales are weak, and telegrams are still scarce. Chinese silk merchants, aware of the general failure of silkworm cocoons in the interior, have become more resolute in their attitude towards holding onto existing silk stocks, resulting in limited transactions. Yesterday, only Anli and others brought in 20 bales of Shanghai white factory silk, and Taihe and others brought in 15 bales of white dried silk. Prices were firm.

The Cocoon Market in Hangzhou and Surrounding Areas Is Quiet

Only 20% of the More Than 200 Cocoon Merchants in the County Are Preparing to Open for Business

In Linping and other areas of Hangzhou, the early silkworms this year completely failed due to the cold weather during the first molt. During the late silkworms' major molt, the weather was extremely cold, with heavy rainfalls causing the silkworms to eat wet leaves, resulting in diarrhea, blackening, red stiffness, and white stiffness, leading to death for about 70% of them. The remaining silkworms are limited in number and are now spinning cocoons. However, the weather remains cold and erratic, with strong winds and heavy rain, creating a poor situation. Silk cocoon merchants are generally taking a passive stance. With the new cocoons soon to be on the market, the cocoon market is quiet. Of the more than 200 cocoon merchants in the county, fewer than 40 have registered and prepared to open for business.

News from Qimen Tea After Its Market Launch Yesterday

The once-renowned Qimen black tea was still being actively sourced by British firms such as Jardine Matheson and Tianyu Dude yesterday. The market momentum was very strong. The entire market traded 2,081 cases of high-grade Qimen tea from the southwest and northern routes, with prices ranging from 240 to 360 taels. Jiande tea prices ranged from 175 to 220 taels. Statistics show that 80% of the tea released the day before had already been sold, indicating strong sales. However, over 7,000 cases arrived in Shanghai by the Yangtze River yesterday, and due to the late arrival, they have not yet been released to the market. Another 7,000 cases are scheduled to arrive, and samples will be released next week, making the market even more lively.

Wenzhou Green Tea Has Opened

Yesterday, the new season of Wenzhou Zhenmei green tea, arriving from other locations, was opened by Tongfu Foreign Firm at 60 taels, with little difference compared to last year. Local Zhuangzhenmei green tea from firms like Jinlong and Jardine Matheson saw some interest yesterday, but bidding became more stringent, and selling prices have already fallen by more than 10 taels. The green tea market does not appear to be optimistic.

Over 400 Tons of Hardware and British Steel Plates Were Fixed

Hardware transactions have been very quiet recently, but sporadic orders are still considerable. Eighteen boxes of green iron wire mesh were opened yesterday at a price of 17.5 taels. Forty to fifty barrels of No. 2 white tinplate were purchased by tea merchants yesterday at a price of 33.5 taels. Although black iron sheets, new zinc wire, I-beams, Tianzi iron, and bamboo joint steel were also offered, the quantity was very small. 7.5-point British steel plates of various colors were traded by Tianjin and Qingdao merchants yesterday, making the market relatively active. However, the inventory has been depleted, so the industry is very active in overseas orders. It is reported that 425 tons were fixed yesterday at a price of 5 pounds and 15 shillings, which is 5 shillings cheaper than before.

The Sugar Market: Increased Transactions in Dutch Sugar Lead to a Sudden Rise in Prices

Japanese Sugar Prices Also Rose Sharply; Shanghai Refinery's Ice Sugar Rose by 2 Qian

Yesterday, according to telegrams from the sugar-producing areas, the current price of Cuban sugar slightly increased by 0.3125. New York sugar futures for May fell by 6 points, September fell by 1 point, December fell by 2 points, and March of next year also fell by 4 points. The current price of Java sugar remained relatively stable. At the beginning of the market opening at the association, the market was only stable, but the asking price was slightly higher by 0.05. Most buyers were still watching. Later, a major firm raised prices and aggressively bought, and the market suddenly became tense. Dutch sugar No. 24 coarse granulated white sugar reached 10 taels and 0.07 yuan; No. 20 medium granulated white sugar reached 10 taels and 0.02 to 0.025 yuan; Dutch red sugar No. 8 reached 9 taels. Transactions were still vigorous, and the trend was outstanding. Taikoo B mark was at 11 taels and 0.05 yuan, DY mark was at 10 taels and 0.065 yuan, and O mark was at 8 taels and 0.085 yuan, with some transactions. Later, sellers raised prices and refused to sell. Japanese sugar N mark was at 10 taels and 0.07 to 0.0775 yuan, TK mark was at 10 taels and 0.075 yuan, YT mark was at 10 taels and 0.06 yuan, up to a maximum of 10 taels and 0.07 yuan, YP mark was at 11 taels to 11 taels and 0.01 yuan, J mark was at 11 taels and 0.01 to 0.05 yuan, YRO mark was at 10 taels to 10 taels and 0.0075 yuan, Minghua goods were at 10 taels and 0.01 yuan, TM mark was at 10 taels and 0.035 to 0.04 yuan. Transactions were quite high, and the market was seen to be rising, with a feeling that prices would soar even further. Transactions in brand-name goods also gradually became more active. Shanghai refinery's ice sugar opened for sale at several hundred packages, Ren mark was at 13 taels and 0.06 yuan, and Qian mark was at 13 taels and 0.05 yuan, which was 0.02 yuan higher than the original price. Ice flower green was priced at 9 taels and 0.05 yuan, and the delivery time was three weeks. The market was still lively. Coarse granulated white Zhenxiang brand opened at over 4,000 bags of high-quality Hong Kong goods at a price of 10 taels and 0.07 yuan. Huaxin also opened at 3,000 bags at a price of 60 taels and 0.07 yuan. At the same time, the company sold over 2,000 bags of medium granulated white sugar at a price of 10 taels and 0.02 yuan. The market trend was firm, which was rare in recent months.
